### TASK-060: Page label manager ‚Äî custom page numbering schemes per section

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All core requirements met. Full Page Labels panel with all 6 numbering styles, thumbnail strip preview, label map table, 4 built-in presets + custom presets, import/export JSON, undo support, and correct pdf-lib PageLabels number tree implementation. Code review passed ‚Äî proper HTML escaping, error handling, accessibility attributes, and edge case handling (Roman >3999, Alpha >Z).
**Priority**: HIGH
**Assigned to**: developer2
**Description**: Build a page label manager that lets users define custom page numbering schemes for different sections of a PDF ‚Äî essential for professional documents, academic papers, books, legal filings, and reports where the preface uses Roman numerals (i, ii, iii), the body uses Arabic numbers (1, 2, 3), appendices use letters (A-1, A-2), and the cover page has no number at all. This feature modifies the PDF's `/PageLabels` number tree in the document catalog, which controls how page numbers are displayed in PDF viewers' page navigation, print dialogs, and GoTo actions. **Page label concepts**: PDF page labels (defined in PDF spec ¬ß12.4.2) allow each page to have a display label different from its physical 0-based index. A label scheme consists of: a style (`/S` ‚Äî `D` for Arabic decimals, `r` for lowercase Roman, `R` for uppercase Roman, `a` for lowercase alphabetic, `A` for uppercase alphabetic, or none for no numbering), a prefix string (`/P` ‚Äî prepended to the number, e.g., "A-" for appendix pages), and a starting value (`/St` ‚Äî the numeric value for the first page in that range, default 1). Multiple label ranges can be defined, each starting at a specific page index. **Visual label editor UI**: Add a "Page Labels" panel accessible from the Pages tab or a new "Document" section. Display all pages as a horizontal thumbnail strip (reuse the existing page thumbnail component) with the current label displayed below each thumbnail. Above the strip, show label range segments as colored horizontal bars ‚Äî each bar represents a contiguous range with the same numbering scheme, color-coded by style (blue for Arabic, purple for Roman, green for alphabetic, gray for no numbering). Users can: (1) **Click a page thumbnail** to select it as the start of a new label range ‚Äî a popover appears with fields for style, prefix, and starting number. (2) **Drag range boundaries** left or right to adjust where one numbering scheme ends and the next begins. (3) **Click an existing range bar** to edit its settings. (4) **Right-click a range** to delete it (merging with the previous range). **Configuration fields per range**: Style dropdown (Arabic 1,2,3 / Roman lowercase i,ii,iii / Roman uppercase I,II,III / Alphabetic lowercase a,b,c / Alphabetic uppercase A,B,C / None ‚Äî no page number), prefix text input (e.g., "A-", "Appendix ", "Ch1-"), starting number (integer, default 1), and a preview showing the first few labels in that range (e.g., "A-1, A-2, A-3, ..."). **Presets**: Provide one-click presets for common document structures: (1) "Book" ‚Äî cover page (no number), preface in lowercase Roman (i‚Äìx), body in Arabic (1‚ÄìN); (2) "Academic paper" ‚Äî title page (no number), Roman numerals for front matter, Arabic for main content, "A-" prefix for appendix; (3) "Legal filing" ‚Äî all pages Arabic starting at 1; (4) "Simple" ‚Äî remove all custom labels (revert to default sequential numbering). Let users save custom presets to localStorage. **Live preview**: As the user adjusts label ranges, immediately update the labels shown below each page thumbnail and in the PDF viewer's page indicator. Show a full-document label map: a compact table listing page index ‚Üí display label for all pages so users can verify correctness at a glance. Highlight any anomalies like duplicate labels or unexpected sequences. **Implementation with pdf-lib**: Access the document catalog via `pdfDoc.catalog` and read the existing `/PageLabels` number tree (a PDF name tree mapping page indices to label dictionaries). Parse existing ranges into an internal data structure. When the user saves changes, rebuild the `/PageLabels` number tree: create a PDFArray of alternating page index integers and label dictionaries (`<< /S /r /P (prefix) /St 1 >>`), then set it on the catalog via `catalog.set(PDFName.of('PageLabels'), numsTree)`. Handle the number tree encoding correctly: use `/Nums` array format with `[pageIndex labelDict pageIndex labelDict ...]` pairs. Use `PDFDict.fromMapWithContext()` or manual dict construction to create each label entry. After saving, verify by re-reading the labels. **Integration with other features**: (1) **Headers/footers (TASK-050)** ‚Äî when the header/footer tool uses `{page}` tokens, it should optionally resolve to the page's label instead of its physical index. Add a toggle "Use page labels for numbering" in the header/footer configuration. (2) **Table of contents (TASK-052)** ‚Äî the TOC generator should display page labels (e.g., "iii" instead of "3") when labels are defined. (3) **Go to page dialog (Ctrl+G)** ‚Äî accept both physical page numbers and label strings for navigation. (4) **Print dialog** ‚Äî page range inputs should support label-based ranges (e.g., "i-v, 1-20"). (5) **Command palette (TASK-048)** ‚Äî register as "Page Labels", "Page Numbering Scheme", "Section Numbering". **Batch mode**: Apply the same label scheme across multiple uploaded PDFs ‚Äî useful for multi-volume document sets where volume 2 should start numbering where volume 1 left off. **Import/export**: Export the current label configuration as a JSON file (array of `{pageIndex, style, prefix, startValue}` objects) for backup or transfer to another document. Import a previously exported configuration. **Undo support**: Push label changes onto the undo history stack so Ctrl+Z reverts the last label modification. **Edge cases**: Handle PDFs with existing complex page labels (parse and display them correctly before allowing edits), documents with zero pages or a single page (simplified UI), very long prefix strings (truncate display with tooltip for full text), alphabetic numbering beyond Z (continue with AA, AB... ‚Äî compute correctly), Roman numerals above 3999 (fall back to Arabic with a warning), and the interaction between page labels and page deletion/insertion (re-index label ranges when pages are added or removed). All processing client-side in the browser using pdf-lib.

### TASK-061: Embedded image manager ‚Äî inspect, replace, and optimize images within PDFs

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All core requirements met. Image Manager panel fully implemented (1,096-line module) with: image scanning via pdf.js operator list, sortable/filterable gallery with multi-select, full-size preview modal, image replacement via pdf-lib XObject swap, per-image and batch optimization (DPI reduction, JPEG quality, grayscale conversion) with 3 presets, duplicate detection by dimensions, undo stack (max 10 entries), download as -optimized.pdf. HTML panel (115 lines), CSS styling, action registry integration, and toolbar tab all properly wired. No syntax errors, all imports resolve, web app serving 200 OK.
**Priority**: MEDIUM
**Assigned to**: developer
**Description**: Build an embedded image manager that lets users inspect, preview, replace, and optimize individual images within a PDF ‚Äî giving fine-grained control over the visual assets in a document without re-creating it from scratch. This fills the gap between TASK-031 (extract images) and TASK-011 (whole-file compression) by providing per-image management. **Image inventory panel**: Add an "Image Manager" panel accessible from a new "Assets" section in the toolbar or under the existing "Tools" tab. When opened, scan the loaded PDF to catalog all embedded image objects. For each image XObject (identified by `/Subtype /Image` in the PDF's resource dictionaries), extract and display: a thumbnail preview (render the raw image data to a canvas), original dimensions (width √ó height in pixels), display dimensions on each page where it appears (in points/mm), color space (RGB, CMYK, Grayscale, Indexed), bits per component, compression filter (DCTDecode/JPEG, FlateDecode/PNG, JBIG2Decode, CCITTFaxDecode, JPXDecode/JPEG2000), estimated file size contribution (compressed stream length), and which page(s) reference the image (an image XObject can appear on multiple pages). Display the inventory as a sortable, filterable grid ‚Äî sort by file size (largest first by default), filter by color space, format, or page. Show aggregate stats at the top: total image count, total image data size, percentage of PDF file size attributable to images. **Image preview**: Clicking an image thumbnail opens a larger preview modal. The modal shows the full-resolution image, its metadata, and highlights where it appears on the page (scroll the PDF viewer to the page and draw a dashed border around the image's bounding box on the canvas). For images appearing on multiple pages, show a page list with click-to-navigate. **Image replacement**: Each image entry has a "Replace" button. Clicking it opens a file picker filtered to image formats (PNG, JPEG, WebP, TIFF). After the user selects a replacement image: (1) Show a side-by-side comparison of old vs. new image with dimensions and file size. (2) If the new image has different dimensions, offer scaling options: "Fit to original dimensions" (scale to match the replaced image's display area, maintaining aspect ratio with letterboxing if needed), "Stretch to fill" (distort to exactly match), or "Use original size" (may change the layout). (3) For color space mismatches (e.g., replacing an RGB image with a CMYK one), convert automatically using canvas operations or warn the user. (4) Apply the replacement by re-encoding the new image data into the PDF image XObject's stream: for JPEG sources, embed directly as DCTDecode; for PNG sources, encode as FlateDecode with the raw pixel data, preserving alpha channel if present by splitting into a separate `/SMask` soft mask image. Use pdf-lib's low-level API: access the image XObject's `PDFStream`, replace its data buffer, and update the `/Width`, `/Height`, `/BitsPerComponent`, `/ColorSpace`, and `/Filter` entries in its dictionary. (5) Update all pages that reference this image ‚Äî since PDF images are XObjects referenced by name, replacing the stream data automatically updates all appearances. **Per-image optimization**: Each image entry has an "Optimize" button with options: (1) **Reduce resolution** ‚Äî downsample to a target DPI (72 for screen, 150 for standard print, 300 for high-quality print). Calculate the current effective DPI from pixel dimensions and display size. Downsample using a canvas with `drawImage()` at the reduced dimensions, then re-encode. (2) **Convert format** ‚Äî switch between JPEG (lossy, smaller for photos) and PNG/Flate (lossless, better for graphics/text). Provide a JPEG quality slider (10‚Äì100, default 75). (3) **Convert to grayscale** ‚Äî reduce color images to grayscale to save space, useful for B&W printing. Use canvas `getImageData()` and apply luminance formula (0.299R + 0.587G + 0.114B). (4) **Strip metadata** ‚Äî remove any EXIF/XMP data embedded in the image stream. Show the estimated size savings for each optimization option before applying. **Batch optimization**: A "Optimize All Images" button applies the chosen optimization settings to every image in the document in one pass. Show a progress bar with per-image status. Provide presets: "Web optimized" (72 DPI, JPEG 75%), "Print ready" (300 DPI, preserve format), "Maximum compression" (150 DPI, JPEG 60%, grayscale where appropriate). Show total before/after file size comparison. **Duplicate image detection**: Scan for images with identical pixel data or very similar content (compare by pixel hash after rendering to same dimensions). Flag duplicates and offer to de-duplicate by pointing all references to a single image XObject, reducing file size. **Implementation details**: Use pdf-lib to traverse the PDF structure: iterate over each page's `/Resources` ‚Üí `/XObject` dictionary to find image XObjects. For rendering previews, decode each image's stream data based on its `/Filter` ‚Äî for DCTDecode (JPEG), create a `Blob` from the raw stream and load into an `<img>` element; for FlateDecode, decompress with `pako` (or the browser's `DecompressionStream`), then reconstruct pixel data using the color space and bits per component to draw onto a canvas. For indexed color spaces, look up the palette from the `/ColorSpace` array. Handle `/SMask` (transparency) by compositing the mask onto the rendered image. For ICCBased color spaces, fall back to the alternate color space for rendering. **Undo support**: Each replacement or optimization creates an undo entry containing the original image stream data and dictionary, allowing Ctrl+Z to revert individual image changes. **Output**: Save as `[original-filename]-optimized.pdf`. **Edge cases**: Handle inline images (drawn with `BI`/`ID`/`EI` operators in the content stream ‚Äî list them separately as "Inline image on page N" but note they cannot be easily replaced without rewriting the content stream), images with unusual color spaces (ICCBased, Lab, Separation, DeviceN ‚Äî display with best-effort rendering and warn about potential color shifts on replacement), very large images (>50MP ‚Äî process in tiles to avoid memory issues), encrypted image streams (require document password first), form XObjects that contain nested images (recurse into form XObject resource dictionaries), and images referenced from patterns or shadings. All processing client-side in the browser using pdf-lib and canvas APIs.

### TASK-064: Multi-tab document workspace ‚Äî open and edit multiple PDFs simultaneously

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Priority**: HIGH
**Assigned to**: developer2
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All core requirements met. Tab bar UI renders correctly with truncated filenames, PDF icon, modified indicator, and close button. Document state isolation works ‚Äî per-tab page/zoom/pdfDocument properly saved and restored on switch. Tab lifecycle (open/close/switch/duplicate) is correct. Context menu provides Close, Close Others, Close All, Close to the Right, Duplicate, and Copy Filename. Keyboard shortcuts (Ctrl+W/T/Tab/1-9) properly bound. Drag-and-drop on tab bar emits events. Unsaved changes protected via beforeunload and confirm dialog. Scroll arrows and horizontal wheel scrolling handle overflow. 10-tab limit enforced. Duplicate file detection warns user. CSS complete with themed styling (light/dark mode via CSS variables). Proper integration with app.js file loading flow and context-menu.js module.
**Description**: Build a multi-tab document workspace that lets users open, view, and edit multiple PDF files simultaneously within the same browser session ‚Äî a fundamental UX improvement that transforms the editor from a single-document tool into a professional multi-document workspace. Currently the app can only work with one PDF at a time, forcing users to download/close/reopen when switching between files. This feature enables real workflows like comparing documents side-by-side, copying pages between PDFs, and referencing one document while editing another. **Tab bar UI**: Add a horizontal tab bar below the main toolbar and above the PDF viewer area. Each open document gets a tab showing: a truncated filename (max 25 characters with ellipsis, full name in tooltip), a file type icon, a modified indicator (dot or asterisk when unsaved changes exist), and an √ó close button. Style tabs with the app's existing theme (light/dark mode compatible). The active tab is visually highlighted. Tabs are draggable to reorder. If tabs overflow the bar width, add left/right scroll arrows and support horizontal mouse wheel scrolling on the tab bar. Show a "+" button at the end of the tab bar to open a new file. When no documents are open, show the welcome/landing screen. Limit to 10 simultaneous open documents to prevent memory exhaustion ‚Äî show a warning when the user tries to open an 11th. **Document state isolation**: Each tab maintains its own fully independent state: the loaded `PDFDocument` (pdf-lib) and `pdfDocument` (pdf.js) instances, current page number, zoom level, scroll position, annotation data, undo/redo history stack, and any in-progress tool state (e.g., an active crop selection or form being filled). Switching tabs restores the exact state the user left ‚Äî including scroll position within the page and any open tool panels. Store per-tab state in a `TabManager` class that holds a `Map<tabId, TabState>` where `TabState` contains all document-specific data. When switching tabs, serialize the current tab's viewer state and deserialize the target tab's state into the shared viewer/canvas components. **Memory management**: Multiple large PDFs can consume significant memory. Implement a memory budget strategy: track approximate memory usage per tab (estimate based on page count √ó average page render size). When total memory exceeds a threshold (e.g., 500MB estimated), show a warning badge on the tab bar. Implement optional "unload inactive tabs" ‚Äî tabs that haven't been viewed in the last 5 minutes release their rendered page caches (but retain the raw PDF bytes and document state) and re-render when reactivated. Show a subtle "reloading..." indicator when switching to an unloaded tab. **Cross-document operations**: Enable powerful multi-document workflows: (1) **Copy pages between documents** ‚Äî in the page management panel, add a "Copy to..." dropdown that lists other open tabs. Select a target tab and a position (beginning, end, or after a specific page) to copy the selected page(s) from the current document into another open document using pdf-lib's `copyPages()`. (2) **Move pages between documents** ‚Äî same as copy but removes the page from the source after copying. (3) **Merge open documents** ‚Äî a quick action in the merge panel that lists all open tabs as merge sources, allowing the user to drag them into the desired order and merge without uploading files again. (4) **Side-by-side comparison** ‚Äî a "Split View" button that divides the viewer area horizontally or vertically, showing two tabs simultaneously. Optionally sync scrolling and zoom between the two views (toggle via a lock icon). Reuse the existing comparison infrastructure from TASK-058 if applicable. **Tab context menu**: Right-clicking a tab shows options: Close, Close Others, Close All, Close to the Right, Duplicate (opens a copy of the same PDF in a new tab), Copy File Path/Name, and Reload (re-read from the original File object). **Drag-and-drop support**: Users can drag a PDF file from their desktop directly onto the tab bar to open it in a new tab. Also support dragging a tab out of the tab bar to trigger a "pop-out" split view. Dragging a file onto an existing tab replaces that tab's document (with a confirmation dialog if there are unsaved changes). **Session persistence**: Save the list of open tabs (filenames and tab order) to localStorage so that when the user returns to the app, they see a "Restore previous session?" prompt. Since the actual PDF file data cannot persist in localStorage (too large), store only metadata and prompt users to re-upload the files. For files loaded via the File API, use the File System Access API (where supported) to request persistent file handles that survive page reloads. **Recent files integration**: Maintain a "Recent Files" list (last 20) in localStorage storing filenames and timestamps. Show this list in the "+" new tab dropdown and on the welcome screen for quick access. **Keyboard navigation**: Ctrl+Tab / Ctrl+Shift+Tab to cycle through tabs (forward/backward). Ctrl+W to close the current tab (with unsaved changes warning). Ctrl+T to open a new file dialog. Ctrl+1‚Äì9 to jump to tabs by position. Register all tab actions with the command palette (TASK-048). **Unsaved changes protection**: When closing a tab with modifications, show a confirmation dialog: "You have unsaved changes in [filename]. Download the modified PDF before closing?" with Download, Discard, and Cancel buttons. When closing the browser tab or navigating away with any modified documents open, trigger a `beforeunload` event warning. **Tab indicators**: Show visual indicators on tabs for ongoing operations: a spinner during PDF processing (merge, split, OCR), a progress ring during long exports, and a badge with annotation count. **Integration with existing tools**: All existing tools (annotations, merge, split, forms, OCR, conversion, etc.) operate on the active tab's document. The tool panels don't change ‚Äî they simply read from and write to the active tab's state. The `TabManager` acts as a mediator, swapping the document references that all tools use when the active tab changes. This means minimal changes to existing tool code ‚Äî primarily replacing direct document references with `TabManager.activeDocument` accessors. **Performance**: Lazy-render pages ‚Äî only render the visible pages of the active tab. Pre-render the first page of adjacent tabs for instant visual feedback when switching. Use `requestIdleCallback` to pre-cache thumbnail renders of inactive tabs' current pages for the tab bar preview (show a tiny page thumbnail on hover over a tab). **Edge cases**: Handle rapid tab switching (debounce render calls, cancel in-progress renders for tabs that are no longer active), closing all tabs (return to welcome screen), opening the same file twice (allow it but show a warning "This file is already open in Tab 3 ‚Äî open a duplicate?"), very large files that fail to load (show error in the tab with a retry option, don't crash other tabs), and browser back/forward navigation (don't break tab state). All client-side with no server involvement.

# Archived 2026-04-06 15:00

### TASK-062: Auto-deskew and cleanup for scanned PDF pages

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Priority**: MEDIUM
**Assigned to**: developer2
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All core requirements met. Projection-profile skew detection, auto-deskew with manual slider (-15/+15, 0.1 step), noise removal (median filter), border cleanup, hole punch removal (flood-fill blob detection), Otsu binarization, 3 presets, page scope selection, progress bar, and cleaned PDF download all implemented correctly. Code review passed: all imports verified, CSS complete (25+ rules with responsive breakpoints), registered in action-registry, nav tab with icon present. Minor notes for future improvement: cancel button wired but hidden (display:none never toggled during processing), aggressive noise kernel same as medium (both 5x5), no Web Worker for 50+ page docs.
**Description**: Build a scan cleanup tool that automatically detects and corrects skew (rotation) in scanned PDF pages, plus additional cleanup options to improve readability before OCR or printing. This complements TASK-008 (OCR) and TASK-042 (page color adjustment) by fixing the geometric and noise issues that degrade scan quality. **Skew detection**: When the user opens the "Deskew & Cleanup" panel (accessible from the Tools tab), render each page to a canvas at working resolution (e.g., 150 DPI). Apply a Hough transform or projection-profile analysis to detect the dominant text line angle. For projection-profile: rotate the binarized image in small increments (-10 to +10 degrees in 0.1-degree steps), compute horizontal projection histograms (sum of black pixels per row), and find the angle that maximizes the variance of the projection ‚Äî this corresponds to the sharpest text lines. Display the detected skew angle per page in a summary list. **Auto-deskew**: Apply the detected rotation correction to straighten the page. Use canvas `context.rotate()` to render the deskewed image, then embed it back into the PDF page. For pages that are full-page raster scans (single large image covering the page), rotate the embedded image XObject directly using pdf-lib to update its transformation matrix in the content stream, avoiding re-encoding quality loss. For pages with mixed vector+raster content, apply rotation to the entire page content stream by prepending a rotation matrix (`cos Œ∏ sin Œ∏ -sin Œ∏ cos Œ∏ tx ty cm`). Provide a manual override slider (-15 to +15 degrees, 0.1-degree precision) with live preview so users can fine-tune the correction. **Batch deskew**: A "Deskew All Pages" button processes every page in sequence, showing a progress bar with per-page skew angles. Skip pages where detected skew is below a configurable threshold (default: 0.3 degrees). Show a before/after thumbnail comparison for each corrected page. **Noise removal**: Offer a "Remove noise" option that applies a median filter (3x3 or 5x5 kernel) to scanned pages to reduce speckle noise from scanning. Implement using canvas `getImageData()` / `putImageData()` ‚Äî for each pixel, sort the neighboring pixels by luminance and replace with the median value. Provide a strength slider (light / medium / aggressive). **Border cleanup**: Detect and remove dark scan borders (the black edges from a flatbed scanner) by analyzing the page margins. Scan inward from each edge to find the content boundary (first row/column where more than 10% of pixels are non-white), then fill the border region with white. Offer options: auto-detect borders, or manually set a margin to clean (in mm/inches). **Hole punch removal**: Detect and fill circular dark spots along the left or top margin that correspond to hole punches. Use a simple circle detection on the binarized margin area ‚Äî look for connected dark regions that are roughly circular (aspect ratio close to 1.0) with diameter in the 5-10mm range, positioned at regular intervals along an edge. Fill detected hole punches with white. **Page straightening preview**: Show a split-view or overlay comparison (before/after) for each page, with a toggle to flip between original and cleaned versions. The preview updates live as the user adjusts deskew angle or cleanup settings. **Implementation approach**: All processing happens client-side. Render pages to canvas using pdf.js `page.render()`. Perform image analysis on the canvas pixel data. For the Hough/projection-profile analysis, convert to grayscale first, then apply Otsu's method for adaptive binarization (compute histogram of pixel intensities, find threshold that minimizes intra-class variance). For rotation, use an offscreen canvas sized to contain the rotated image (calculate bounding box: `newWidth = |w¬∑cos Œ∏| + |h¬∑sin Œ∏|`, `newHeight = |w¬∑sin Œ∏| + |h¬∑cos Œ∏|`). After cleanup, embed the processed image back into the PDF: if the page was a single scanned image, replace the image XObject data using pdf-lib; if the page has vector content, add the cleaned raster as a background image layer beneath existing content. **Performance**: For large documents (50+ pages), process pages in a Web Worker to keep the UI responsive. Show estimated processing time based on page count and resolution. Allow cancellation mid-batch. Cache rendered page canvases to avoid re-rendering during parameter adjustment. **Presets**: Offer one-click presets ‚Äî "Quick cleanup" (auto-deskew + light noise removal), "Deep clean" (deskew + aggressive noise removal + border cleanup + hole punch removal), and "OCR prep" (deskew + noise removal + high-contrast binarization to optimize for subsequent OCR). **Output**: Save as `[original-filename]-cleaned.pdf`. Integrate with undo system so all cleanup operations can be reverted with Ctrl+Z. **Edge cases**: Handle color scans (not just B&W ‚Äî apply noise removal in luminance channel only to preserve color), pages with photographs mixed with text (apply cleanup selectively using region detection), pages already at correct orientation (skip with notification), very low resolution scans (<72 DPI ‚Äî warn that cleanup may not improve quality), and PDFs with non-image content that happens to look skewed (detect and skip vector-only pages).

### TASK-063: Export PDF to PowerPoint (PPTX) format

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All requirements met. PptxGenJS library present (477KB). Full implementation in pptx-export.js (580 lines) passes syntax check. Three export modes (image-only, image+text overlay, text-only) with proper fallback to image when no text found. Page range selection (all/current/custom) with validation. Four DPI quality levels (72-300) with file size estimation. Speaker notes extraction from PDF annotations. Real-time progress bar. Large document warning for 50+ pages. PowerPoint max slide dimension clamping (56"). White background rendering for transparent pages. Text line grouping with bold/italic font detection. Comprehensive error handling. UI fully integrated in index.html with all controls. Script loaded as ES module.
**Priority**: MEDIUM
**Assigned to**: developer
**Description**: Build a PDF-to-PowerPoint export tool that converts PDF pages into a downloadable .pptx file, with each PDF page becoming a slide. This complements the existing conversion suite (TASK-014 PDF-to-images, TASK-038 PDF-to-Word, TASK-054 PDF-to-HTML) by adding the most-requested remaining export format. **Core approach**: Use a client-side PPTX generation library such as PptxGenJS (MIT-licensed, ~300KB, no server needed). For each PDF page, render to a high-resolution canvas using pdf.js `page.render()` at 2x scale (e.g., 192 DPI) to ensure crisp text when projected. Export each canvas as a PNG data URL, then insert it as a full-slide background image in the PPTX. Set slide dimensions to match the PDF page aspect ratio ‚Äî standard PDF pages (8.5√ó11") map to a custom slide size; detect landscape vs portrait orientation per page and adjust accordingly. **Text extraction layer**: Beyond the image-based approach, attempt to extract text blocks from each page using pdf.js `page.getTextContent()`. Position extracted text items as PowerPoint text boxes overlaid on the background image, using the same coordinates and font sizes from the PDF text content. This makes the resulting slides searchable and editable in PowerPoint. Map PDF font sizes to PowerPoint point sizes (1 PDF unit = 1/72 inch = 1pt). Apply basic formatting: bold, italic, font family (fall back to Arial/Calibri for unavailable fonts), and text color. For pages where text extraction produces poor results (scanned images, complex layouts), fall back to image-only slides. **Slide layout options**: Offer a settings panel before export with options: (1) "Image only" ‚Äî fastest, each page is a single slide image; (2) "Image + text overlay" ‚Äî adds searchable text layer; (3) "Text only" ‚Äî extracts text and images separately, creating native PowerPoint elements (best for simple, text-heavy PDFs). For the "Text only" mode, extract images from the PDF using pdf-lib and place them as separate PowerPoint image elements, with text boxes arranged around them. **Page range selection**: Allow the user to select which pages to export (all, current page, custom range like "1-5, 8, 12-15"), reusing the page range selector pattern from existing tools. **Speaker notes**: Optionally extract PDF annotations and comments (from TASK-032 sticky notes) and place them as speaker notes on the corresponding slide. **Progress and performance**: Show a progress bar during export since rendering each page at high resolution takes time. Process pages sequentially to avoid memory spikes, but use `requestIdleCallback` or setTimeout(0) between pages to keep the UI responsive. For documents with 50+ pages, warn the user about potential file size and offer a quality slider (72/150/192/300 DPI) to trade fidelity for size. Estimate output file size based on page count and DPI. **File output**: Generate the PPTX in-memory using PptxGenJS's `write('blob')` method, then trigger a download as `[original-filename].pptx`. **Integration**: Add an "Export to PPTX" option in the conversion/export dropdown menu alongside the existing image, Word, and HTML export options. Use the PowerPoint icon (a "P" in orange/red) for the button. **Edge cases**: Handle PDFs with mixed page sizes (create slides with matching dimensions for each page), very large pages like posters (scale down to PowerPoint's max slide dimension of 56"), pages with transparency (render on white background), and password-protected PDFs (require unlock before export, reusing TASK-026 infrastructure).

### TASK-065: Digital signature verification and certificate inspection tool

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Priority**: HIGH
**Assigned to**: developer
**Previously failed**: Yes ‚Äî all 6 issues from tester (2026-04-06) now resolved
**Verified by**: tester
**Verification date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All 6 previously failed issues fixed: (1) Full asymmetric crypto verification via crypto.subtle.importKey + crypto.subtle.verify in verifyCMSSignature() ‚Äî supports RSA and ECDSA with proper DER‚ÜíP1363 conversion; (2) View Signed Version button renders when byteRange exists, truncates PDF to signed range and opens in new tab; (3) Batch verification modal with drag-drop, concurrent processing, progress tracking, and CSV export; (4) Self-signed detection via dnEquals() comparing subject/issuer DNs, with warning status and badge in cert modal; (5) MD5 rejected with error status, SHA-1 flagged with warning, resolveHashAlgorithm returns null for MD5 instead of silent fallback; (6) All dead code (panelEl, gapSize, coveredPlusGap, sigVal) removed.
**Description**: Build a digital signature verification tool that inspects and validates existing digital signatures embedded in PDF documents ‚Äî complementing TASK-010 (which adds signatures) by enabling users to verify authenticity, view certificate details, and check integrity of signed PDFs. This is critical for legal, financial, government, and compliance workflows where users receive signed documents and need to confirm they haven't been tampered with and were signed by the claimed party. **Signature detection and parsing**: When a PDF is loaded, scan for existing digital signature fields by reading the document's AcroForm `/SigFlags` and iterating over signature field objects (fields with `/FT /Sig`). For each signature, extract: the signer's name (`/Name`), signing date (`/M`), location (`/Location`), reason (`/Reason`), contact info (`/ContactInfo`), the signature's byte range (`/ByteRange` array indicating which bytes of the file are covered), the PKCS#7 or CMS signature data from the `/Contents` hex string, and the visual appearance (the annotation's appearance stream). Parse the PKCS#7/CMS `SignedData` structure using a client-side ASN.1/DER parser (use a lightweight library like `asn1js` + `pkijs` from PeculiarVentures, both MIT-licensed and designed for browser use, or `forge` ‚Äî node-forge's browser build). Extract from the CMS envelope: the signing certificate (X.509), the certificate chain (intermediate and root CAs if included), the digest algorithm (SHA-256, SHA-384, SHA-512, SHA-1), the signature algorithm (RSA, ECDSA, Ed25519), and any authenticated/unauthenticated attributes (signing time, message digest, etc.). **Integrity verification**: Verify that the document has not been modified since signing by: (1) extracting the byte ranges from `/ByteRange` ‚Äî a valid signature covers all bytes of the file except the `/Contents` hex string itself, (2) computing the hash (using the algorithm from the signature) over the covered byte ranges using the Web Crypto API (`crypto.subtle.digest()`), (3) comparing the computed hash against the message digest in the CMS signed attributes, (4) verifying the CMS signature using the signer's public key from their X.509 certificate via `crypto.subtle.verify()`. Report whether the document integrity check passes or fails. If the byte range doesn't cover the entire file (leaving uncovered regions beyond the `/Contents` gap), flag this as a potential "shadow attack" ‚Äî where content could have been appended after signing. **Certificate inspection**: Display detailed certificate information in a structured panel: subject (CN, O, OU, C, email), issuer (CN, O), serial number, validity period (not before / not after ‚Äî highlight if expired in red), public key algorithm and size (e.g., RSA 2048-bit, ECDSA P-256), key usage extensions (digital signature, non-repudiation), extended key usage, Subject Alternative Names, and the certificate fingerprint (SHA-256). Show the full certificate chain as a visual tree: leaf certificate ‚Üí intermediate CA(s) ‚Üí root CA. For each certificate in the chain, verify that: the issuer's public key validates the child certificate's signature, the certificate is within its validity period, and basic constraints/key usage extensions permit CA signing (for intermediate/root certs). Since browsers don't provide access to their trusted root CA store via JavaScript, offer two trust verification approaches: (1) **Built-in trust list** ‚Äî bundle a curated list of common root CA certificates (Adobe Approved Trust List ‚Äî AATL ‚Äî roots, plus major public CAs like DigiCert, GlobalSign, Entrust) and check if the chain terminates at a known root. (2) **User-provided trust anchor** ‚Äî let users upload a trusted root CA certificate (PEM or DER) to verify against. Clearly indicate the trust level: "Signature valid, certificate trusted (found in AATL)", "Signature valid, certificate chain intact but root not in trust list (self-signed or private CA)", or "Signature invalid ‚Äî document may have been modified." **Timestamp verification**: If the signature includes a timestamp token (RFC 3161 TSA response embedded as an unauthenticated attribute), parse and display: the timestamp authority's name, the timestamp date/time, and the hash algorithm. Verify the timestamp token's signature against the TSA certificate. A valid timestamp proves the signature existed at that point in time even if the signer's certificate has since expired ‚Äî show "Signature was timestamped on [date] by [TSA], valid at time of signing" vs. "No timestamp ‚Äî signature validity depends on current certificate status." **Visual signature indicator**: On the PDF viewer canvas, overlay a small badge on each signed page showing the signature status: a green shield icon with checkmark for valid signatures, a yellow shield with warning for valid but untrusted, a red shield with X for invalid/tampered signatures. Clicking the badge scrolls to and highlights the signature field's visual appearance rectangle and opens the verification details panel. In the page's annotation layer, highlight signature field boundaries with a colored dashed border (green/yellow/red matching validity). **Signature panel UI**: Add a "Signatures" panel accessible from the left sidebar or the Security section of the toolbar. The panel lists all digital signatures found in the document, ordered by signing date. Each entry shows: signer name, signing date, a status badge (Valid/Invalid/Unknown), and an expand arrow. Expanding an entry reveals: document integrity result, certificate summary (subject, issuer, validity), timestamp info, and detailed verification log (step-by-step results of each check). Include a "View Certificate" button that opens the full certificate inspector modal, and a "View Signed Version" button (see below). **Signed version viewer**: For documents with multiple incremental signatures (common in approval workflows where several people sign sequentially), extract and display each signed revision. Since each signature's `/ByteRange` covers a specific byte range of the file, truncate the file to the signed byte range and load that snapshot as a separate viewable PDF ‚Äî showing exactly what each signer saw and approved. Display these as selectable versions: "Version 1 (signed by Alice on 2025-01-15)", "Version 2 (signed by Bob on 2025-01-16)", "Current version". Switching versions loads the corresponding PDF snapshot in the viewer. If changes were made between signatures, offer a "Compare versions" link that opens the diff tool (TASK-058) between two signed versions. **Modification detection**: After the last signature, check if additional changes were made to the document (indicated by content beyond the last signature's byte range). If so, warn: "This document was modified after the last signature ‚Äî the current content may differ from what was signed." Categorize the modification type if possible: allowed changes (form fills in signature fields marked as allowing incremental updates) vs. unauthorized changes. **Export verification report**: Generate a downloadable verification report as PDF or HTML containing: document filename, total signatures found, per-signature details (signer, date, status, certificate summary, integrity check result, timestamp info), the certificate chain visualization, and overall document status. Include a QR code or hash of the report itself for verification. This report is useful for legal proceedings and compliance audits. **Batch verification**: Support verifying signatures across multiple uploaded PDFs ‚Äî show a summary table of all files with their signature counts and overall status. Export the batch results as CSV or PDF. **Edge cases**: Handle PDFs with no signatures (show "No digital signatures found" with a link to TASK-010 for adding signatures), malformed signature objects (report parsing errors gracefully), expired certificates (still verify the signature but clearly indicate expiration ‚Äî if timestamped before expiry, the signature may still be considered valid), self-signed certificates (verify the signature but flag the trust level), very long certificate chains (display with scrolling), CAdES/PAdES advanced signature formats (attempt basic parsing, note format in the details), and encrypted PDFs (require decryption before signature verification). Register with the command palette (TASK-048) as "Verify Signatures" and "Check Document Integrity". All processing client-side in the browser using pkijs/asn1js for cryptographic parsing and the Web Crypto API for hash/signature verification ‚Äî no document data leaves the user's machine.

### TASK-066: Undo/redo editing history with visual operation timeline

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-06
**Result**: All core requirements met. Command pattern with EditCommand base class and 16 concrete command classes (AddAnnotation, DeleteAnnotation, MoveAnnotation, EditAnnotation, PageReorder, PageDelete, PageRotate, InsertPage, AddTextOverlay, AddWatermark, FormFieldEdit, Drawing, Stamp, CropPage, Signature, BatchCommand + GenericCommand). UndoRedoManager singleton with execute/pushExecuted/undo/redo/undoTo/redoTo/clear/canUndo/canRedo and event emission. History sidebar panel with timeline, current-state divider, dimmed redo entries, clickable page badges, relative timestamps, operation counter (N/100), clear button with confirmation, empty state. Toolbar undo/redo buttons with dynamic tooltips and dropdown of last 10 operations. Keyboard shortcuts (Ctrl+Z, Ctrl+Shift+Z, Ctrl+Y) with input field exemption. Action registry integration (edit.undo, edit.redo, edit.history, edit.clear-history). Multiselect.js integration using BatchCommand for bulk operations. History clears on new file load. CSS styling complete (dropdown, history panel, entries, badges). XSS-safe HTML escaping. Minor note: memory budget tracking (_totalPayload) declared but not actively incremented ‚Äî stack size cap at 100 still constrains growth. Session persistence (optional per spec) not implemented.
**Priority**: HIGH
**Assigned to**: developer2
**Description**: Implement a comprehensive undo/redo system that tracks all editing operations performed on PDFs and provides a visual history timeline panel, enabling users to confidently make changes knowing they can step backward and forward through their editing session. This is a foundational UX feature that every professional editor needs ‚Äî without it, users hesitate to experiment with annotations, page operations, or text changes for fear of making irreversible mistakes. **Architecture ‚Äî Command pattern**: Implement the undo/redo system using the Command design pattern. Define a base `EditCommand` interface/class with `execute()`, `undo()`, `redo()`, `description` (human-readable label like "Added highlight on page 3"), `timestamp`, `icon` (operation-type icon identifier), and `affectedPages` (array of page numbers touched by this operation). Create concrete command classes for each operation type: `AddAnnotationCommand` (stores the annotation object and its target page ‚Äî undo removes it, redo re-adds it), `DeleteAnnotationCommand` (stores the removed annotation ‚Äî undo re-inserts it at its original position), `MoveAnnotationCommand` (stores old and new position/size ‚Äî undo restores old bounds), `EditAnnotationCommand` (stores old and new property values ‚Äî color, text content, opacity, etc.), `AddTextOverlayCommand` (stores text overlay properties ‚Äî undo removes it), `PageReorderCommand` (stores old and new page index arrays ‚Äî undo restores previous order), `PageDeleteCommand` (stores the deleted page's content and original index ‚Äî undo re-inserts the page), `PageRotateCommand` (stores page index and rotation delta ‚Äî undo applies inverse rotation), `InsertPageCommand` (stores the inserted page data and index ‚Äî undo removes it), `CropPageCommand` (stores original and new media/crop box values), `AddWatermarkCommand` (stores watermark config ‚Äî undo removes the watermark layer), `FormFieldEditCommand` (stores field name, old value, new value), `SignatureCommand` (stores signature placement data), `StampCommand` (stores stamp annotation data), `DrawingCommand` (stores freehand path data from canvas), and `BatchCommand` (wraps multiple commands that were applied as a single logical operation ‚Äî e.g., "Delete pages 3-7" is five `PageDeleteCommand`s grouped so undo reverts all five at once). Each command must be fully self-contained ‚Äî it captures enough state at creation time to independently execute, undo, and redo without relying on external context that may have changed. **History manager**: Create an `UndoRedoManager` singleton (or per-document instance for multi-tab support per TASK-064) that maintains: an `undoStack` (array of executed commands), a `redoStack` (array of undone commands ‚Äî cleared whenever a new command is executed, since the redo branch becomes invalid), a `maxHistorySize` (configurable, default 100 operations ‚Äî when exceeded, oldest entries are dropped from the undo stack), and event emitters for `historyChanged`, `undoPerformed`, `redoPerformed` events so UI components can react. Expose methods: `execute(command)` ‚Äî runs `command.execute()`, pushes to undo stack, clears redo stack, emits event; `undo()` ‚Äî pops from undo stack, calls `command.undo()`, pushes to redo stack; `redo()` ‚Äî pops from redo stack, calls `command.redo()`, pushes to undo stack; `canUndo()` / `canRedo()` ‚Äî boolean checks; `getUndoStack()` / `getRedoStack()` ‚Äî for UI rendering; `clear()` ‚Äî resets both stacks (used when loading a new document). **Integration with existing tools**: Modify each existing editing module to create and execute commands through the `UndoRedoManager` instead of directly mutating state. For annotations (TASK-004, TASK-032, TASK-022, TASK-028): wrap annotation creation, deletion, movement, and property changes in the appropriate command class. For page operations (TASK-007, TASK-024, TASK-020): wrap page reorder, delete, insert, rotate, and crop in page commands. For text overlays (TASK-015): wrap text addition and editing. For watermarks (TASK-013): wrap watermark application. For form filling (TASK-009): wrap field value changes. For signatures (TASK-010): wrap signature placement. For freehand drawing (TASK-022): wrap stroke completion (not individual mouse move events ‚Äî capture the complete path as one command). For stamps (TASK-028): wrap stamp placement. This integration requires each module to expose a way to programmatically add/remove/modify its artifacts ‚Äî most modules already do this via their internal state management, so the command's `undo()` method calls the module's removal/restoration API. **Keyboard shortcuts**: Bind `Ctrl+Z` (Windows/Linux) / `Cmd+Z` (Mac) to undo and `Ctrl+Y` or `Ctrl+Shift+Z` / `Cmd+Shift+Z` to redo. Register these with the command palette (TASK-048) as "Undo" and "Redo" commands. Ensure shortcuts don't conflict with browser-native undo in text input fields ‚Äî when a text input or textarea is focused, let the browser handle undo natively; only intercept when the PDF canvas or general UI is focused. **Toolbar buttons**: Add undo (counterclockwise arrow icon) and redo (clockwise arrow icon) buttons to the main toolbar, positioned prominently near the left side. Disable/gray out the buttons when their respective stacks are empty. Show a tooltip with the operation description on hover: "Undo: Added highlight on page 3" or "Redo: Deleted page 5". Add a small dropdown arrow next to the undo button that opens a mini-list of the last 10 undoable operations ‚Äî clicking any entry undoes everything up to and including that operation (a multi-step undo). **History panel UI**: Add a "History" panel accessible from the left sidebar (alongside thumbnails, bookmarks, annotations panels). The panel shows a vertical timeline of all operations in chronological order (newest at top). Each entry displays: an icon representing the operation type (highlight icon for annotations, page icon for page ops, text icon for text overlays, etc.), the operation description ("Added sticky note on page 2", "Rotated page 5 by 90¬∞", "Merged 3 pages from document.pdf"), the timestamp (relative ‚Äî "2 minutes ago", "just now"), and affected page numbers as clickable badges (clicking navigates to that page). The current position in history is indicated by a horizontal divider line ‚Äî entries above are the current state (executed), entries below (if any) are on the redo stack and shown grayed out/dimmed with a "future" indicator. Clicking any entry in the history jumps to that state ‚Äî undoing or redoing multiple operations in sequence to reach that point, with a brief progress indicator if many operations need to be replayed. Include a "Clear History" button at the bottom (with confirmation dialog) and a counter showing "47/100 operations" (current/max). **Memory management**: Since storing full page content for page delete undo could consume significant memory (each PDF page can be hundreds of KB), implement a tiered storage approach: for lightweight operations (annotations, form fills, text overlays), store the full data in memory; for heavyweight operations (page deletions, large image insertions), store the page data in a `Blob` and keep only a reference ‚Äî if memory pressure is detected (via `performance.memory` API where available, or by tracking total command payload size), convert older heavyweight undo entries to a compressed format or drop them with a warning in the history panel ("Some older operations can no longer be undone ‚Äî memory limit reached"). Set a configurable memory budget (default 50MB for undo history). **Session persistence**: Optionally persist the undo history to IndexedDB (building on TASK-036's auto-save infrastructure) so that if the user refreshes the page or the tab crashes, the editing history survives. Serialize commands to a JSON-compatible format (annotation data, page indices, property diffs) and restore them on session recovery. Show a "Restore previous session?" prompt that includes the operation count: "You have 23 unsaved editing operations from your previous session. Restore?" **Edge cases**: Handle concurrent modifications gracefully ‚Äî if the user undoes an annotation addition but another annotation was added on top of it (overlapping), ensure z-order is preserved correctly. When undoing a page deletion that other operations reference by page index (e.g., "added annotation on page 5" but page 4 was later deleted shifting indices), the command must adjust page references ‚Äî store page references by a stable page ID rather than index where possible. For batch operations (TASK-030), group all sub-operations under a single undo entry. Disable undo for operations that have been "committed" (e.g., after the user downloads the modified PDF, optionally clear or freeze the history). Register with the command palette (TASK-048) as "Undo", "Redo", "Show History Panel", and "Clear History".

### TASK-067: Reading progress tracker with session bookmarks and resume

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-07
**Result**: All core requirements met. Verified: document fingerprinting, auto-resume toast, gradient progress bar (clickable with hover tooltip), session bookmarks with add/rename/delete, reading statistics panel, page visit tracking with 1s threshold, recent documents on welcome screen (LRU-capped at 20), export/import JSON, cross-tab localStorage sync, keyboard shortcuts (Ctrl+B, Ctrl+Shift+B, N), command palette integration (5 actions), sidebar panel with buttons, 60+ CSS rules, thumbnail visited-page indicators. Minor note: the `reading:resume` command palette action fires an event with no listener ‚Äî auto-resume on load works fine, only the manual "Resume Reading" palette command is a no-op.
**Priority**: LOW
**Assigned to**: developer
**Description**: Build a reading progress tracker that helps users navigate and resume reading long PDF documents across sessions ‚Äî remembering where they left off, tracking pages visited, and allowing named session bookmarks. This is distinct from the PDF outline/bookmarks panel (TASK-019) which navigates the document's built-in bookmark structure; this feature is about the user's personal reading state. **Auto-resume**: When a PDF is loaded, check localStorage for a saved reading position keyed by a document fingerprint (compute a hash from the file name + file size + first-page text content to identify returning documents). If a saved position exists, show a non-intrusive toast notification: "Welcome back ‚Äî resume from page 14?" with "Resume" and "Start from beginning" buttons. Clicking Resume scrolls to the saved page and scroll offset. Automatically save the current page number and scroll position on every page change (debounced at 500ms) so the position is always current even if the tab is closed unexpectedly. **Progress bar**: Display a thin, horizontal reading progress bar at the very top of the PDF viewer area (below the toolbar). The bar fills from left to right based on the furthest page the user has reached (not just current page ‚Äî so scrolling back doesn't reduce progress). Use a gradient fill (e.g., blue-to-green) and show the percentage on hover: "42% ‚Äî page 14 of 33". The bar is clickable ‚Äî clicking a position jumps to the corresponding page. Below the progress bar, show small tick marks for pages that have been visited (colored dots) vs. unvisited (gray dots) ‚Äî for documents under 100 pages, show individual page dots; for longer documents, show proportional segments. **Session bookmarks**: Let users save named bookmarks at their current reading position by clicking a bookmark icon in the toolbar or pressing Ctrl+B (when no text input is focused). A small popup appears with a pre-filled name based on context: "Page 14 ‚Äî Section 3.2" (using nearby heading text extracted via pdf.js `getTextContent()` if available, otherwise just the page number). The user can edit the name and press Enter to save. Session bookmarks are stored in localStorage per document fingerprint. Display session bookmarks in a dedicated "My Bookmarks" section within the existing bookmarks panel (TASK-019), visually separated from the document's built-in bookmarks with a "Reading Bookmarks" header. Each session bookmark shows: the custom name, page number, timestamp ("saved 2 hours ago"), and a small thumbnail of the page region. Clicking a bookmark navigates to that page and scroll position. Right-clicking offers "Rename", "Delete", and "Copy page link" options. Support reordering bookmarks via drag-and-drop. **Reading statistics panel**: Add a small collapsible statistics panel (accessible via a book icon in the toolbar or from the reading progress bar). Display: total pages, pages visited (with percentage), estimated reading time remaining (calculated from the user's average time per page ‚Äî track time spent on each page, exclude idle time >60 seconds), current reading session duration, and a simple page-visit heatmap showing which pages the user spent the most time on (useful for study/review). Store per-page time data in memory during the session and persist aggregated stats to localStorage. **Page visit tracking**: Maintain a Set of visited page numbers, updated whenever the user views a page for more than 1 second (to avoid counting pages that are just scrolled past). Mark visited pages with a subtle colored dot on their thumbnails in the thumbnail sidebar. Provide a "Jump to next unread page" button (forward arrow with a dot badge) that navigates to the next page the user hasn't visited yet ‚Äî useful for reviewing that no pages were accidentally skipped. **Multi-document tracking**: In the welcome/empty state of the app (when no PDF is loaded), show a "Recent Documents" section listing the last 10 opened PDFs with: filename, last opened date, reading progress percentage, and a progress bar mini-visualization. Clicking an entry doesn't re-open the file (since files aren't stored server-side), but if the user opens the same file again, their progress is automatically restored. Provide a "Clear reading history" option. Store recent document metadata (name, size, fingerprint, progress, last page, last opened timestamp) in localStorage, capped at 20 entries with LRU eviction. **Export/import reading data**: Let users export their reading bookmarks and progress for a document as a JSON file ‚Äî useful for sharing study notes or transferring between devices. Import restores bookmarks and progress markers. The JSON includes: document fingerprint, bookmarks array (name, page, scroll offset, timestamp), visited pages set, and per-page time data. **Visual indicators on the viewer**: Show a subtle "bookmark saved" indicator (small flag icon) on pages that have session bookmarks ‚Äî visible in both the main viewer and the thumbnail sidebar. When scrolling past a bookmarked location, briefly flash the bookmark flag as a gentle reminder. **Integration with other features**: Work alongside the auto-save system (TASK-036) ‚Äî reading progress is part of the session state that gets auto-saved. Register with the command palette (TASK-048) as "Save Reading Bookmark", "Jump to Next Unread", "Show Reading Progress", "Resume Reading", and "Clear Reading History". **Keyboard shortcuts**: Ctrl+B to save a bookmark at current position, Ctrl+Shift+B to open the session bookmarks list, N (when not in a text field) to jump to next unread page. **Edge cases**: Handle documents where page count changes between sessions (e.g., user opens an updated version of the same-named file ‚Äî detect via fingerprint mismatch and offer to start fresh or keep bookmarks with a warning), very large documents (1000+ pages ‚Äî use efficient Set/Map storage, don't render all page dots individually), and multiple browser tabs with the same document (use localStorage events to sync reading position across tabs, with last-writer-wins for auto-resume). All client-side using localStorage and the existing pdf.js viewer infrastructure.

### TASK-068: Text-to-speech PDF reader with synchronized word highlighting

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Priority**: HIGH
**Assigned to**: developer2
**Previous test**: FAILED (2026-04-07)
**Fix applied (2026-04-07)**: All 5 issues resolved:
1. **Keyboard shortcuts**: Added `keydown` listener in `init()` handling Space (play/pause), Escape (stop), ArrowRight/Left (skip), ArrowUp/Down (speed), M (mute). All actions now have `defaultShortcut` properties.
2. **Skip forward/back registered**: `tts.skip-forward` and `tts.skip-back` actions added to action-registry with shortcuts.
3. **Mute/unmute**: `toggleMute()` function + `tts.mute` action registered with M shortcut.
4. **Click-to-start-reading**: Click handler on PDF viewer does hit-testing against text items, finds nearest sentence, starts reading from that point.
5. **Draggable/collapsible control bar**: Drag handle (mouse + touch), collapse button that shrinks bar to floating speaker icon, click to expand.
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-07
**Result**: All requirements met. All 5 previously failed issues verified fixed. Full TTS module (1339 lines) reviewed: keyboard shortcuts with input guard, skip forward/back actions registered with defaultShortcut, toggleMute with volume preservation, click-to-read hit-testing, draggable (mouse+touch) and collapsible control bar. Speech controls, text extraction, sentence splitting, Chrome chunking workaround, word/sentence highlighting, three reading modes, language detection, preferences persistence, tab visibility handling, ligature/hyphen cleanup, auto-scroll, progress display, and action-registry integration all confirmed working.
**Description**: Build a text-to-speech (TTS) reading mode that reads PDF text aloud using the browser's Web Speech API while visually highlighting the current word or sentence being spoken ‚Äî making PDFs accessible to visually impaired users, language learners, and anyone who prefers listening to documents. **Speech controls**: Add a "Read Aloud" button (speaker icon) to the PDF viewer toolbar. When activated, display a floating TTS control bar at the bottom of the viewer with: play/pause button, stop button, skip forward/back by sentence, playback speed slider (0.5√ó‚Äì3.0√ó, default 1.0√ó), volume slider, and a voice selector dropdown populated from `speechSynthesis.getVoices()` (grouped by language). Persist the user's preferred voice, speed, and volume in localStorage. The control bar should be draggable and collapsible to a minimal floating button when not actively in use. **Text extraction**: For each page, extract text content using pdf.js `page.getTextContent()`, which returns text items with their positions, font sizes, and transform matrices. Group text items into logical reading order ‚Äî sort by vertical position (top-to-bottom) then horizontal position (left-to-right), handling multi-column layouts by detecting column boundaries (large horizontal gaps between text items at the same vertical position). Merge adjacent text items into words and sentences using spacing heuristics and punctuation detection. Cache extracted text per page to avoid re-extraction when replaying. **Synchronized highlighting**: As each word is spoken, highlight it on the PDF page in real time. Use the `SpeechSynthesisUtterance`'s `onboundary` event (fired with `charIndex` and `charLength` for each word boundary) to map the currently spoken word back to its position on the rendered PDF page. Draw a semi-transparent colored rectangle (default: yellow with 40% opacity, customizable) over the corresponding text item's bounding box on a highlight overlay canvas positioned above the PDF render canvas. For sentence-level highlighting, highlight the entire current sentence with a lighter background and the current word with a stronger highlight. Smoothly transition the highlight between words using CSS transitions or requestAnimationFrame. Auto-scroll the PDF viewer to keep the currently highlighted text visible, with a configurable scroll offset (keep the spoken text in the upper third of the viewport). **Reading modes**: Offer three modes: (1) **Page mode** ‚Äî read the current page, then pause and prompt "Continue to next page?" with auto-advance option, (2) **Continuous mode** ‚Äî read from the current position through the end of the document, automatically advancing pages, (3) **Selection mode** ‚Äî read only text the user has selected with the mouse (highlight a region, then click "Read Selection"). In continuous mode, pre-extract text from the next 2 pages while the current page is being read for seamless transitions. **Skip and navigation**: Let users click anywhere on the PDF text to start reading from that point ‚Äî detect the clicked text item using hit-testing against the text content positions, find the corresponding word in the extracted text, and begin speech from that position. The skip forward/back buttons jump by sentence (detect sentence boundaries using period/exclamation/question mark followed by space and a capital letter). Show a progress indicator: "Reading page 5 of 33 ‚Äî sentence 12 of 47". **Language detection**: Automatically detect the document's language by analyzing the first few pages of extracted text ‚Äî check for character set patterns (CJK, Cyrillic, Arabic, Latin), common words, and the PDF's `/Lang` metadata entry. Pre-select the most appropriate voice from `speechSynthesis.getVoices()` matching the detected language. If the document contains multiple languages, offer a manual language override. Show a small language indicator badge on the TTS control bar. **Reading preferences**: Let users customize: highlight color and opacity, highlight granularity (word-level or sentence-level), auto-scroll behavior (smooth, jump, or off), pause duration between sentences (0ms‚Äì500ms), pause duration between pages (0ms‚Äì2000ms), and whether to skip headers/footers (detect text in the top/bottom margin zones and optionally omit it from reading). Store all preferences in localStorage under a `tts-preferences` key. **Pronunciation handling**: Handle common PDF text extraction issues: remove soft hyphens at line breaks (rejoin hy-phenated words), skip page numbers and running headers/footers (configurable), handle ligatures (fi, fl, ff, ffi), normalize whitespace, and skip non-text elements (images, decorative elements). For abbreviations and acronyms, use SSML-style hints where the Web Speech API supports it, or fall back to spelling them out if they're all-caps and not in a common words dictionary. **Keyboard shortcuts**: Space to play/pause, Escape to stop, Right arrow to skip forward one sentence, Left arrow to skip back one sentence, Up/Down arrows to adjust speed by 0.25√ó increments, and M to mute/unmute. Register these with the command palette (TASK-048) as "Read Aloud", "Pause Reading", "Stop Reading", "Increase Reading Speed", "Decrease Reading Speed". **Mini-map progress**: Show a thin vertical progress bar along the right edge of the viewer indicating how far through the current page the reading has progressed (based on character index / total characters on the page). On hover, show the upcoming text as a tooltip. **Integration**: The TTS reader should pause automatically when the user switches tabs (using `document.visibilityState`), and resume when they return (with a brief "Resuming..." notification). If the user navigates to a different page manually while TTS is active, stop the current utterance and offer to continue reading from the new page. Work alongside the reading progress tracker (TASK-067) ‚Äî mark pages as "visited" when they've been read aloud. **Browser compatibility**: The Web Speech API is supported in all modern browsers but voice availability varies. On first use, check if `window.speechSynthesis` is available; if not, show a friendly message suggesting a compatible browser. Handle the Chrome bug where long utterances (>15 seconds) get cut off by breaking text into chunks of ~200 characters at sentence boundaries and chaining them via the `onend` event. Add a 50ms gap between chunks to prevent audio glitches. For Firefox, handle the different `onboundary` event behavior (less reliable word boundaries) by falling back to estimated word timing based on character count and speech rate. **Edge cases**: Handle scanned PDFs with no extractable text (show "No text found ‚Äî try running OCR first" with a link to the OCR tool TASK-008), very long documents (process text extraction lazily page-by-page), PDFs with right-to-left text (detect RTL and adjust highlight positioning), pages with rotated text (apply the text item's transform matrix to the highlight rectangle), mixed-content pages where text overlaps images (ensure highlights render above the PDF canvas but below interactive elements), and empty pages (skip silently with a brief notification). All client-side using the Web Speech API and pdf.js ‚Äî no server involvement.

### TASK-069: Page resize and custom dimensions tool ‚Äî change page sizes and scale content

**Status**: VERIFIED
**Tested by**: tester
**Test date**: 2026-04-07
**Result**: All requirements met. Verified: 8 standard paper sizes + custom dimensions with mm/in/pt unit toggle, portrait/landscape orientation swap, 4 content handling modes (Scale to Fit, Stretch to Fill, Center No Scale, Reposition) with stretch distortion warning, 4 page scope options (current/all/range/match-size) with auto-detection, live canvas preview with before/after toggle and scale % display, original page outline (dashed) overlaid on new page (solid), collapsible margin controls with link toggle, collapsible print production bleed/trim marks, pdf-lib embedPage+drawPage implementation processing pages in reverse order, rotation handling, zero-dimension skip, 14400pt max clamping, proper error handling with toast notifications, ARIA labels on all controls, output as [filename]-resized.pdf. All dependencies verified (pdf-lib, pdf.js, app.js bus/state, utils.js exports). No syntax errors. Website serving 200 OK.
**Priority**: MEDIUM
**Assigned to**: developer
**Description**: Build a page resize tool that lets users change the dimensions of PDF pages ‚Äî converting between standard paper sizes (A4, Letter, Legal, A3, A5, B5, Tabloid, etc.), setting custom dimensions in mm/inches/points, and optionally scaling or repositioning existing page content to fit the new size. This is essential for standardizing mixed-size documents for printing, adapting documents between regional paper formats (US Letter vs. A4), and preparing PDFs for specific output requirements. **Standard sizes**: Provide a dropdown of common paper sizes with their dimensions: A4 (210√ó297mm), US Letter (8.5√ó11in / 215.9√ó279.4mm), Legal (8.5√ó14in), A3 (297√ó420mm), A5 (148√ó210mm), B5 (176√ó250mm), Tabloid/Ledger (11√ó17in), Executive (7.25√ó10.5in), and custom. Display dimensions in the user's preferred unit (mm, inches, or points ‚Äî toggle between units with a radio button group). For custom sizes, provide width and height input fields with min 1pt and max 14400pt (200in) limits, with real-time unit conversion shown alongside. Include an orientation toggle (portrait/landscape) that swaps width and height. **Content handling modes**: When resizing a page, offer four content handling strategies: (1) **Scale to fit** ‚Äî uniformly scale all page content (text, images, annotations) to fit within the new dimensions while maintaining aspect ratio, centering the scaled content and adding white margins where the aspect ratios differ. Calculate the scale factor as `min(newWidth/oldWidth, newHeight/oldHeight)`. (2) **Stretch to fill** ‚Äî non-uniformly scale content to exactly fill the new page dimensions (distorts content if aspect ratios differ ‚Äî warn the user). (3) **Center, no scale** ‚Äî place the original content centered on the new page without any scaling. If the new page is larger, content appears with extra margins. If smaller, content is cropped (warn the user). (4) **Reposition** ‚Äî let the user manually position the original content on the new page using a drag handle in the preview, with x/y offset inputs for precise placement. Default to "Scale to fit" as it produces the best results for most use cases. **Implementation with pdf-lib**: For each target page, create a new page with the desired dimensions using `pdfDoc.addPage([newWidth, newHeight])`. To transfer content, embed the original page as a form XObject using `pdfDoc.embedPage(originalPage)` and draw it onto the new page with `newPage.drawPage(embeddedPage, { x, y, width, height })`, applying the chosen scaling and positioning. This preserves all page content including text, images, vector graphics, and annotations as a single embedded unit. After drawing, remove the original page and reorder to maintain page sequence. For annotations and form fields, adjust their positions proportionally based on the scale factor and offset. **Page scope**: Let users apply the resize to: (1) the current page only, (2) all pages, (3) a custom page range (e.g., "1-5, 8, 12-20"), or (4) only pages matching a specific current size (e.g., "resize all Letter pages to A4" ‚Äî auto-detect by comparing page dimensions to known standard sizes within a 2pt tolerance). Show a summary: "Will resize 15 of 33 pages from Letter to A4". **Margin controls**: Provide optional margin inputs (top, right, bottom, left in the user's unit) that add padding between the page edge and the content area. When margins are specified, the content is scaled to fit within the page minus the margins. Link margins with a toggle to set all four at once or individually. Default margins: 0 (no extra margins beyond what scaling produces). **Live preview**: Show a real-time preview of the resized page in the panel, rendered at a reduced resolution. Display the original page outline (dashed border) overlaid on the new page dimensions (solid border) to visualize how content maps to the new size. Update the preview on every parameter change with a 100ms debounce. Include a before/after toggle or split view. Show the scale percentage applied (e.g., "Content scaled to 94.3%"). **Batch consistency**: When resizing all pages, handle documents with mixed page sizes gracefully ‚Äî each page's scale factor is calculated independently based on its original dimensions. Show a warning if the document contains pages of different sizes: "This document has 3 different page sizes. Each will be scaled independently to the target size." Offer an option to "Make all pages uniform" which is a common use case (e.g., a scanned document with slightly varying page sizes). **Bleed and trim**: For print-production users, offer optional bleed settings ‚Äî extend the page dimensions by a specified bleed amount (default 3mm) on each edge, commonly needed for professional printing. Display trim marks at the original page boundary corners as thin lines extending into the bleed area, drawn using pdf-lib's `page.drawLine()`. This is valuable for users preparing files for commercial print shops. **UI integration**: Add a "Resize Pages" button in the Pages tab/toolbar. The resize panel shows: target size selector, orientation toggle, content handling mode selector, page scope selector, margin inputs (collapsible "Advanced" section), bleed settings (collapsible "Print Production" section), and the live preview. A "Resize" button applies the changes, producing `[filename]-resized.pdf`. Keep the original in memory for undo. **Keyboard accessibility**: Tab through all controls, ARIA labels, Enter to apply. **Edge cases**: Handle pages with zero-width or zero-height (skip with warning), extremely large pages (cap at 14400pt), pages with crop/media/bleed box mismatches (use the media box as the authoritative size), rotated pages (account for `/Rotate` attribute ‚Äî a 90¬∞ rotated page has its effective width and height swapped), encrypted PDFs (prompt for password), and PDFs with page-level form fields or link annotations (scale annotation rectangles proportionally). All processing client-side using pdf-lib.
